  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1965969547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1965969547" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1965969547?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8257073-going-postal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1965969547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9328150743655143522"><i>Going Postal</i> is the first book in the <i>Moist von Lipwig</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>, which is also associated with the <i>Industrial Revolution</i> subseries. In the case of this book, it’s maybe a little more of an “Industrial Counterrevolution”.<br/><br/>The post office in Ankh-Morpork has effectively been out of commission for a while, with tons of undelivered letters sitting around. Meanwhile, over the past several books, we’ve seen the development of a faster and more efficient method of communication called the </span>
  <span id="freeText9328150743655143522" style="display:none"><i>Going Postal</i> is the first book in the <i>Moist von Lipwig</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>, which is also associated with the <i>Industrial Revolution</i> subseries. In the case of this book, it’s maybe a little more of an “Industrial Counterrevolution”.<br /><br />The post office in Ankh-Morpork has effectively been out of commission for a while, with tons of undelivered letters sitting around. Meanwhile, over the past several books, we’ve seen the development of a faster and more efficient method of communication called the “Clacks”. However, lately there have been issues with the Clacks -- mismanagement, downtime, and maybe even murders.<br /><br />The main character, Moist von Lipwig, was a fun character of the “lovable rogue” archetype. I wasn’t too sure about him at first, but he grew on me as the book went on. Vetinari also had some good moments in this book. The story itself held my interest really well. In fact, I think this may be the first <i>Discworld</i> book for which I actually stayed up a few minutes past my bedtime one night because I wanted to know what would happen next. I only stayed up about 15 minutes late, but I take my bedtime very seriously so this isn’t a common occurrence for me. :) <br /><br />I enjoyed the ending, and I particularly liked the choices Moist made it the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[To be more specific, I liked that he looked at the bigger picture and considered the greater good. He backed off from his original plan that would have effectively destroyed the Clacks until they could be rebuilt, realizing that they fulfill a vital role and also that there were a lot of good people involved in the industry who would suffer. Instead, he found a way to deal with the corrupt management that was the root problem. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="9328150743655143522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3635345225" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3635345225" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5261455-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506384653p2/5261455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3635345225?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/5261455-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5261455-caroline?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3635345225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11288404177693426486">The protagonist reflects on his new assignment: making the collapsing clacks (telegraph) system viable, as he has the post office.<br/><br/><blockquote>He would have to keep the trunk running, gods knew how. He’d sort of promised the gnu, hadn’t he? And it was amazing how people had come to rely on the clacks. … But it was a big, cumbersome monster of a thing, too many towers, too many people, too much effort. There had to be a way of making it better, and sleeker, and cheaper. Or maybe it was so big that no one coul</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11288404177693426486" style="display:none">The protagonist reflects on his new assignment: making the collapsing clacks (telegraph) system viable, as he has the post office.<br /><br /><blockquote>He would have to keep the trunk running, gods knew how. He’d sort of promised the gnu, hadn’t he? And it was amazing how people had come to rely on the clacks. … But it was a big, cumbersome monster of a thing, too many towers, too many people, too much effort. There had to be a way of making it better, and sleeker, and cheaper. Or maybe it was so big that no one could run it at a profit. Maybe it was like the post office, maybe the profit turned up spread all over society.</blockquote><br /><br />Well, yes. We have just had a massive demonstration of the full value of the post office doing its job, even if it's running at a loss. Because its externalities are priceless. And of registrars of voters and secretaries of state and clerks doing their jobs, meticulously and responsibly. Even if these organizations don’t make a profit and seem awfully old fashioned.<br /><br />This was an excellent book to read amid the fireworks and ticking off of firsts. I loved reading it amid the announcements of plans to return to functioning public services.<br /><br />Pratchett has written an entertaining skewering of what happens when neoliberals gut corporations, and manage communications companies that ought to serve the public. He writes about the everyday employees and small business people who get steamrollered in the interest of profits.<br /><br />But the cleverest part is, his protagonist is a con man who has never thought about the consequences of his scams on the people he cheats. Until he meets one of them. Suddenly his only chance at survival is to make a moribund post office viable again. To his surprise, the challenge of using psychology to accomplish something good turns out to be as exciting as using it to sell fake diamond rings.<br /><br /> Moist gives lectures throughout about how to put over a con. He explains how to use people’s suspicions. He also uses these skills throughout, although with ever-increasing unease. It’s like, say, reading ‘The Art of the Deal’ and then watching the author running the con in plain sight for five years: explaining what he does, and then doing it with great success, ruining the very people who read it without them suspecting a thing. Or rather, as Moist says, a part of them know he’s doing it, but the bigger part keeps hoping that they really can buy a diamond ring for $14.95.<br /><br />Moreover, the protagonist makes the reader reflect on the small errors or oversights that have turned out to his or her benefit, and undoubtedly cost someone something. <br /><br />There are morally ambiguous, or rather realistic, parts at the end. Big Finance has to be called in to keep things running when the ‘too big to fail’ villains go down. (Yes, it’s a spoiler, but not really in a Terry Pratchett novel.) The protagonist has to use assertion and show-business film-flam to accomplish the big spin in the dénouement, because the facts aren’t quite there, at least in time. When are compromises necessary?<br /><br />I am now firmly on the Terry Pratchett bandwagon. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11288404177693426486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6771431'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6771431-terry-pratchett-s-hogfather"><img alt="Terry Pratchett&#39;s Hogfather: The Illustrated Screenplay" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348554026l/6771431._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7vE+D0ofQgMDwNFCL2Bu+5Gb01ZGaJJTJ4ZhyTHOv8HU11fd8UGLa6TrZSPYlWQkR8Q0nojlHDR8+Cd4/I1NWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HAplhIdbJ81IchCqAMnG/9p1QCmkIpqxSM1RIEYFv4YmLAxWPAXupe9ZpMv3PMwgDCqn4WqvFNYTsxeRi0ZNHA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

In the background beat the new rhythms of urban experience: the coming and going of the latest planes and trains and automobiles, the clacking of typewriters in vast offices, the jazz band that never sleeps. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15422360704619157960">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText15422360704619157960" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
